## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (mass-action rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard object modeled in chemical kinetics via ordinary differential equations. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are single-species effective rate laws (decay, autocatalysis, inhibition, reversible relaxation) possibly with time-varying rate coefficients.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption, e.g., catalyst-saturated regime)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order decay (single-species effective): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction or lumped kinetics)
- General nth-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Production with decay (source + sink): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant feed or generation balanced by first-order loss)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium (linear driving force): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to steady-state/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type mass action): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-catalysis with limiting reagent/effective carrying capacity)
- Inhibited/limited-rate consumption (rational): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (self-inhibition or limited active sites; effective rate saturation in A)
- Competitive inhibition-like higher-order rational: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (stronger inhibition/crowding at high A)
- Time-dependent first-order (aging catalyst / changing conditions): dA_dt = -A * (c0 + c1 * t) (rate coefficient drifting approximately linearly with time)
- Periodic forcing of rate (e.g., pulsed illumination/temperature cycling): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 + sin(c2 * t)) (externally modulated kinetics)
- Stretched-exponential kinetics (distributed rate constants): dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (effective kinetics from heterogeneity; hazard increases/decreases with time)
- Autocatalysis with inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 - A) / (A + c3) (growth promoted by A but curtailed by depletion/inhibition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Single-reactant consumption under mass action often yields dA_dt proportional to -A**n; the fitted exponent indicates effective reaction order (nâ‰ˆ1 unimolecular, nâ‰ˆ2 bimolecular, non-integer for complex mechanisms).
- If A approaches a nonzero steady value, include a driving-force term (c - A) rather than pure decay; this represents relaxation to equilibrium/steady state.
- Autocatalysis typically introduces a factor A multiplying the net driving force, giving dA_dt ~ A*(c - A); this creates slow start (near Aâ‰ˆ0) and faster mid-course rates.
- Observed slowdown at high A can indicate self-inhibition/crowding; rational forms like A/(A+c) or A/(c + A + c*A^2) capture decreasing marginal rate with A.
- A constant source term (Â±c0) is a signature of feed/zero-order generation, photochemical constant flux, or boundary-controlled supply dominating the kinetics.
- Time-dependent rate coefficients (k(t)) are suggested when dA_dt vs A is not single-valued over t (hysteresis in Aâ€“dA_dt); include polynomial-in-t or sinusoidal modulation of the effective rate.
- If early-time behavior differs markedly from late-time at similar A, incorporate explicit t factors multiplying A (e.g., t**p * A) to represent catalyst deactivation/activation or transport regime changes.
- Sign changes in dA_dt (switch from production to consumption) are consistent with relaxation-to-setpoint forms c*(cA - A) or source-minus-sink structures c0 - c1*A rather than pure -A**n.
